<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the islands of the sovereign state, see <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(Antilles)" title="Saint Vincent (Antilles)">Saint Vincent (Antilles)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a>.</div>

<a href="/wiki/.vc" title=".vc">.vc</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɡ/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">ɡ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/En-us-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Saint Vincent and the Grenadines.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> <a href="/wiki/Island_arc" title="Island arc">island arc</a>, in the southern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a>, which lies in the West Indies at the southern end of the eastern border of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> where the latter meets the Atlantic Ocean. The country is also <a href="/wiki/Pars_pro_toto#Geography" title="Pars pro toto">known simply as</a> <b>Saint Vincent</b>.
</p><p>Its 389&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (150&#160;sq&#160;mi) territory consists of the main island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(Antilles)" title="Saint Vincent (Antilles)">Saint Vincent</a> and the northern two-thirds of the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a>, which are a chain of smaller islands stretching south from Saint Vincent Island to <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>. Most of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines lies within the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Belt" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Belt">Hurricane Belt</a>.
</p><p>To the north of Saint Vincent lies <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, to the east <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>. Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is a densely populated country (over 300 inhabitants/km<sup>2</sup>) with approximately 109,643 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kingstown" title="Kingstown">Kingstown</a> is the capital and main port. Saint Vincent has a <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> colonial history and is now part of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">CARICOM</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alliance_for_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas">Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States" title="Community of Latin American and Caribbean States">Community of Latin American and Caribbean States</a> (CELAC).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The main mother tongue is <a href="/wiki/Vincentian_Creole" title="Vincentian Creole">Vincentian Creole</a> and the official language is English.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(October 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="History of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">History of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_settlements">Early settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The island now known as Saint Vincent was originally named <i>Youloumain</i><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> by the native <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a> who called themselves Kalina/Carina ("l" and "r" being pronounced the same in their language). The Caribs aggressively prevented European settlement on Saint Vincent until 1719. Prior to this, formerly enslaved <a href="/wiki/Africans" class="mw-redirect" title="Africans">Africans</a>, who had either been <a href="/wiki/Shipwreck" title="Shipwreck">shipwrecked</a> or who had escaped from <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> and sought refuge in mainland Saint Vincent, <a href="/wiki/Interracial_marriage" title="Interracial marriage">intermarried</a> with the Caribs and became known as <a href="/wiki/Black_Carib" title="Black Carib">Black Caribs</a> or <a href="/wiki/Garifuna_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Garifuna people">Garifuna</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="French_colony_.E2.80.93_First_phase"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colony_–_First_phase">French colony – First phase</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: French colony – First phase">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first Europeans to occupy St. Vincent were the French. Following a series of wars and peace treaties,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (March 2018)">which?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> the islands were eventually ceded to the British. While the English were the first to lay claim to St Vincent in 1627, the French centred on the island of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> would be the first European settlers on the island when they established their first colony at <a href="/wiki/Barrouallie" title="Barrouallie">Barrouallie</a> on the Leeward side of St Vincent in 1719.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The French settlers cultivated coffee, tobacco, <a href="/wiki/Indigo" title="Indigo">indigo</a>, corn, and sugar<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> on plantations worked by African slaves.
</p>
<h3><span id="British_colony_.E2.80.93_First_phase"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colony_–_First_phase">British colony – First phase</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: British colony – First phase">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg/170px-SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg" width="170" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg/255px-SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg/340px-SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="760" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depiction of the 1773 treaty negotiations between the British and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Carib" title="Black Carib">Black Caribs</a></div></div></div>
<p>The British captured the island from the French during the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years&#39; War">Seven Years' War</a> fought between 1754 and 1763. St Vincent was ceded to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris (1763)</a>, after which friction between the British and the Caribs led to the <a href="/wiki/First_Carib_War" title="First Carib War">First Carib War</a>. On taking control of the island in 1763, the British laid the foundations of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Charlotte,_Saint_Vincent" title="Fort Charlotte, Saint Vincent">Fort Charlotte</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="French_colony_.E2.80.93_Second_phase"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colony_–_Second_phase">French colony – Second phase</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: French colony – Second phase">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The island was <a href="/wiki/French_capture_of_Saint_Vincent" class="mw-redirect" title="French capture of Saint Vincent">restored to French rule in 1779</a> and regained by the British under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles_(1783)" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Versailles (1783)">Treaty of Versailles (1783)</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="British_colony_.E2.80.93_Second_phase"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colony_–_Second_phase">British colony – Second phase</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: British colony – Second phase">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between 1783 and 1796, there was again conflict between the British and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Carib" title="Black Carib">Black Caribs</a>, who were led by Paramount Chief <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Chatoyer" title="Joseph Chatoyer">Joseph Chatoyer</a>. Between 1795 and 1796, with French support from <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, the Black Caribs fought a series of battles against the British. Their uprising was eventually put down, resulting in almost 5,000 Black Caribs being exiled to the tiny island of <a href="/wiki/Baliceaux" title="Baliceaux">Baliceaux</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Bequia" title="Bequia">Bequia</a>.
</p><p>Conflict between the British and the Black Caribs continued until 1796. In 1797 British General Sir <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Abercromby" title="Ralph Abercromby">Ralph Abercromby</a> put an end to the open conflict by <a href="/wiki/Second_Carib_War" title="Second Carib War">crushing an uprising</a> which had been supported by the French radical, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugues" title="Victor Hugues">Victor Hugues</a>. The British deported more than 5,000 Black Caribs to <a href="/wiki/Roat%C3%A1n" title="Roatán">Roatán</a>, an island off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>.
</p><p>In 1806 the building of Fort Charlotte was completed.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/La_Soufri%C3%A8re_(volcano)" title="La Soufrière (volcano)">La Soufriere volcano</a> erupted in 1812.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_(1907-1979).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_(1907-1979).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Colonial flag (to 1979)</div></div></div>
<p>Like the French before them, the British also used African slaves to work plantations of sugar, coffee, indigo, tobacco, cotton and cocoa until full emancipation in 1838. The economy then went into a period of decline with many landowners abandoning their estates and leaving the land to be cultivated by liberated slaves.
</p><p>Slavery was <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">abolished</a> in Saint Vincent (as well as in the other British colonies) in 1834, and an apprenticeship period followed which ended in 1838. After its end, labour shortages on the plantations resulted, and this was initially addressed by the immigration of indentured servants. In the late 1840s many Portuguese immigrants arrived from <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and between 1861 and 1888 shiploads of East Indian labourers arrived. Conditions remained harsh for both former slaves and immigrant agricultural workers, as depressed world sugar prices kept the economy stagnant until the turn of the century.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_and_21st_centuries">20th and 21st centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 20th and 21st centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png/220px-Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png/330px-Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png/440px-Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png 2x" data-file-width="496" data-file-height="494" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Residents of Saint Vincent making <a href="/wiki/Tapioca#Flatbreads" title="Tapioca"><i>casabe</i></a> (casava bread) in the 1910s</div></div></div>
<p>In 1902, <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_(volcano)" class="mw-redirect" title="Soufrière (volcano)">La Soufrière volcano</a> erupted, killing 2,000&#160;people. Much farmland was damaged, and the economy deteriorated.
</p><p>From 1763 until its independence in 1979, Saint Vincent and the Grenadines passed through various stages of colonial status under the British. A representative assembly was authorized in 1776, Crown Colony government was installed in 1877, a <a href="/wiki/Legislative_council" title="Legislative council">legislative council</a> was created in 1925, and <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal adult suffrage</a> was granted in 1951.
</p><p>During the period of its control of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines, the British made several unsuccessful attempts to affiliate the island with other Windward Islands. This would have simplified Britain's control over the region through a unified administration. In the 1960s, several regional islands under British control, including Saint Vincent, also made an independent attempt to unify. The unification was to be called the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> and was driven by a desire to gain freedom from British rule. The attempt collapsed in 1962.
</p><p>Saint Vincent was granted "associate statehood" status by Britain on 27 October 1969. This gave Saint Vincent complete control over its internal affairs but was short of full independence. On 27 October 1979, following a referendum<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> under <a href="/wiki/Milton_Cato" title="Milton Cato">Milton Cato</a>, Saint Vincent and the Grenadines became the last of the Windward Islands to gain independence. Independence came on the 10th anniversary of Saint Vincent's associate statehood status.
</p><p>In April 1979, La Soufrière erupted again. Although no one was killed, thousands were evacuated, and again there was extensive agricultural damage. In 1980 and 1987, hurricanes damaged many banana and coconut plantations. Hurricane seasons were also very active in 1998 and 1999, with <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</a> in 1999 causing extensive damage to the west coast of the island.
</p><p>On 25 November 2009, voters were asked to approve a new constitution in a <a href="/wiki/Vincentian_constitutional_referendum,_2009" title="Vincentian constitutional referendum, 2009">referendum</a>. The new constitution proposed to make the country a republic and replacing Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as head of state with a non-executive President. A two-thirds majority was required, and it was defeated by 29,019 votes (55.64 per cent) to 22,493 (43.13 per cent).<sup id="cite_ref-antillean_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-antillean-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Geography of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Geography of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg/220px-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg.png" width="220" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg/330px-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg/440px-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="612" data-file-height="792" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent Island">Saint Vincent</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a></div></div></div>
<p>Saint Vincent and the Grenadines lies to the west of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> and north of <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Island_arc" title="Island arc">island arc</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. The islands of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines include the main island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent (island)">Saint Vincent</a> 344&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (133&#160;sq&#160;mi) and the northern two-thirds of the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a> 45&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (17&#160;sq&#160;mi), which are a chain of smaller islands stretching south from Saint Vincent to Grenada. There are 32 islands and cays that make up St Vincent and the Grenadines (SVG). Nine are inhabited, including the mainland St Vincent and the Grenadines islands: Young Island, <a href="/wiki/Bequia" title="Bequia">Bequia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mustique" title="Mustique">Mustique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canouan" title="Canouan">Canouan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_Island" title="Union Island">Union Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayreau" title="Mayreau">Mayreau</a>, Petit St Vincent and Palm Island. The capital of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is <a href="/wiki/Kingstown" title="Kingstown">Kingstown</a>, Saint Vincent.
</p><p>The main island of Saint Vincent measures 26&#160;km (16&#160;mi) long, 15&#160;km (9.3&#160;mi) in width and 344&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (133&#160;sq&#160;mi) in area. From the most northern to the most southern points, the Grenadine islands belonging to Saint Vincent span 60.4&#160;km (37.5&#160;mi) with a combined area of 45&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (17&#160;sq&#160;mi).
</p><p>The island of Saint Vincent is volcanic and includes little level ground. The windward side of the island is very rocky and steep, while the leeward side has more sandy beaches and bays.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Saint Vincent's highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_(volcano)" class="mw-redirect" title="Soufrière (volcano)">La Soufrière volcano</a> at 1,234&#160;m (4,049&#160;ft).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Politics of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Politics of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ralph_Gonsalves_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg/190px-Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="190" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg/285px-Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg/380px-Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1762" data-file-height="1492" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ralph_Gonsalves_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Current Prime Minister of St. Vincent and the Grenadines since 2001 <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Gonsalves" title="Ralph Gonsalves">Ralph Gonsalves</a></div></div></div>
<p>Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">constitutional monarchy</a> with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> as head of state, bearing the title <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Monarchy of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Queen of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>. The Queen does not reside in the islands and is represented in the country by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors-General_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors-General of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Governor General of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, currently Sir <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Ballantyne" title="Frederick Ballantyne">Frederick Ballantyne</a>.
</p><p>The office of Governor General has mostly ceremonial functions including the opening of the islands' <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="House of Assembly of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">House of Assembly</a> and the appointment of various government officials. Control of the government rests with the elected <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="List of Prime Ministers of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Prime Minister</a> and his or her cabinet. The current Prime Minister is <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Gonsalves" title="Ralph Gonsalves">Ralph Gonsalves</a>, elected in 2001 as head of the <a href="/wiki/Unity_Labour_Party" title="Unity Labour Party">Unity Labour Party</a>.
</p><p>The legislative branch of government is the unicameral <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="House of Assembly of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">House of Assembly of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, seating 15 elected members representing single-member <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">constituencies</a> and six appointed members known as <i>Senators</i>. The parliamentary term of office is five years, although the Prime Minister may call elections at any time.
</p><p>The judicial branch of government is divided into district courts, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Caribbean_Supreme_Court" title="Eastern Caribbean Supreme Court">Eastern Caribbean Supreme Court</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Privy Council">Privy Council</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> being the court of last resort.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The two political parties with parliamentary representation are the <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_(Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines)" title="New Democratic Party (Saint Vincent and the Grenadines)">New Democratic Party</a> (NDP) and the <a href="/wiki/Unity_Labour_Party" title="Unity Labour Party">Unity Labour Party</a> (ULP). The parliamentary opposition is made up of the largest minority stakeholder in the general elections, headed by the <a href="/wiki/Opposition_(parliamentary)" title="Opposition (parliamentary)">leader of the opposition</a>. The current opposition leader is Dr. Godwin Friday.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Military of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Military of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<p>Saint Vincent has no formal armed forces, although the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Police_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Saint Vincent and the Grenadines Police Force">Royal Saint Vincent and the Grenadines Police Force</a> includes a Special Service Unit as well as a militia that has a supporting role on the island.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Parishes of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Parishes of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<p>Administratively, Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is divided into six <a href="/wiki/Parish_(country_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Parish (country subdivision)">parishes</a>. Five parishes are on Saint Vincent, while the sixth is made up of the Grenadine islands. <a href="/wiki/Kingstown" title="Kingstown">Kingstown</a> is located in the Parish of Saint George and is the capital city and central administrative centre of the country.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental_health">Mental health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Mental health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2016, Saint Vincent and the Grenadines launched a nationwide initiative to improve the psychological wellness and mental health of the population. <b>The Psychological Wellness Initiative</b> is believed to be the first comprehensive mental health service of its type in the world. This represents an open access, upstream, national programme that is made available online and free-of-charge to individual citizens. This initiative comprises three online programmes for anxiety, low mood and workplace stress, based on <a href="/wiki/Acceptance_and_commitment_therapy" title="Acceptance and commitment therapy">Acceptance and Commitment Therapy</a> (ACT). The ACT programmes are provided by Anglo-Finnish innovators Headsted Limited <sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and are sponsored by the European Union as part of the 10th <a href="/wiki/European_Development_Fund" title="European Development Fund">European Development Fund</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: LGBT rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="LGBT rights in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">LGBT rights in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<p>Homosexuality is illegal in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines. Section 148 of the Criminal Code states that "Any person, who in public or private, commits an act of gross indecency with another person of the same sex, or procures or attempts to procure another person of the same sex to commit an act of gross indecency with him or her, is guilty of an offence and liable to imprisonment for five years".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Foreign relations of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Foreign relations of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_and_regional_relationships">International and regional relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: International and regional relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Saint Vincent and the Grenadines maintains close ties to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">US</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and cooperates with regional political and economic organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS) and <a href="/wiki/CARICOM" class="mw-redirect" title="CARICOM">CARICOM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ird.gov.tt_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ird.gov.tt-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_.28CARICOM.29_Treaty"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_(CARICOM)_Treaty">The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 6 July 1994 at Sherbourne Conference Centre, St. Michael, Barbados,  as a representative of the Government of St. Vincent and the Grenadines, then (James Mitchell, who was subsequently knighted) signed the Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaties.<sup id="cite_ref-ird.gov.tt_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ird.gov.tt-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> There were seven other signatories to the agreement on that day. The countries which were represented were: Antigua and Barbuda, Belize, Grenada, Jamaica, St. Kitts and Nevis, St. Lucia, and Trinidad and Tobago.
</p><p>An eighth country signed the agreement on 19 August 2016, Guyana.
</p><p>This treaty covered taxes, residence, tax jurisdictions, capital gains, business profits, interest, dividends, royalties and other areas.<sup id="cite_ref-ird.gov.tt_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ird.gov.tt-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FATCA">FATCA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: FATCA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 30 June 2014, St. Vincent and the Grenadines signed a Model 1 agreement with the United States of America with respect to Foreign Account Tax Compliance (Act) or FATCA.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the updated site as of 16 January 2017, on 13 May 2016 the agreement went to "In Force" status.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_and_regional_bodies_to_which_St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_belong">International and regional bodies to which St. Vincent and the Grenadines belong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: International and regional bodies to which St. Vincent and the Grenadines belong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>St Vincent and the Grenadines is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a> (ACS).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_of_American_States">Organisation of American States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Organisation of American States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Charter of the OAS was signed in Bogota in 1948 and was amended by several Protocols which were named after the city and the year in which the Protocol was signed, such as "Managua" in "1993" forming part of the name of the Protocol.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>St. Vincent and the Grenadines entered the OAS system on 27 October 1981 according to the OAS website.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Summits_of_the_Americas">Summits of the Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Summits of the Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The  last Summits of the Americas, the seventh, was held in Panama City, Panama in 2015 with the eight summit being held in Lima, Peru in 2018 according to the website of the Summits of Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span id="Indigenous_Leaders_Summits_of_Americas_.28ILSA.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_Leaders_Summits_of_Americas_(ILSA)">Indigenous Leaders Summits of Americas (ILSA)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Indigenous Leaders Summits of Americas (ILSA)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>With St Vincent and the Grenadines having  at least two groups of indigenous persons <sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> it is expected that there will be contributions from the SVG's on this topic at the next ILSAs.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The position of the OAS with respect to indigenous persons appears to be developing over the years. The following statements appear to capture the position of  the OAS with respect to the ILSA: "The OAS has supported and participated in the organisation of Indigenous Leaders Summits of Americas (ILSA)" according to the OAS's website. The most recent "statement made by the Heads of State of the hemisphere was in the Declaration of Commitments of Port of Spain  in 2009 – Paragraph 86 according to the OAS's website."<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Draft American Declaration of the Rights of the Indigenous Persons appear to be a working document. The last "Meeting for Negotiations in the Quest for Consensus on this area appeared to be Meeting Number (18) eighteen and is listed as being held in May 2015 according to the website."<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_nations">European nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: European nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, Saint Vincent called for European nations to pay reparations for the slave trade.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Saint Vincent protests <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>'s claim to give full effect to <a href="/wiki/Aves_(Bird)_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Aves (Bird) Island">Aves (Bird) Island</a>, which creates a Venezuelan <a href="/wiki/EEZ" class="mw-redirect" title="EEZ">EEZ</a>/<a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelf</a> extending over a large portion of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Economy of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Economy of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png/220px-St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png/330px-St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png/440px-St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="855" data-file-height="668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of St Vincent and the Grenadines' exports</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent,_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent,_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kingstown, St. Vincent</div></div></div>
<p>Agriculture, dominated by banana production, is the most important sector of this lower-middle-income economy. The services sector, based mostly on a growing tourist industry, is also important. The government has been relatively unsuccessful at introducing new industries, and the <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Unemployment rate">unemployment rate</a> remains high at 19.8% in the 1991 census<sup id="cite_ref-popin_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popin-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> to 15% in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The continuing dependence on a single crop represents the biggest obstacle to the islands' development as tropical storms wiped out substantial portions of bananas in many years.
</p><p>There is a small manufacturing sector and a small offshore financial sector whose particularly restrictive secrecy laws have caused some international concern.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In addition, the natives of <a href="/wiki/Bequia" title="Bequia">Bequia</a> are permitted to hunt up to four <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whales</a> per year under <a href="/wiki/International_Whaling_Commission" title="International Whaling Commission">IWC</a> subsistence quotas.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The tourism sector has considerable potential for development. The recent filming of the <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirates of the Caribbean films">Pirates of the Caribbean</a></i> movies on the island has helped to expose the country to more potential visitors and investors. Recent growth has been stimulated by strong activity in the construction sector and an improvement in tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-sids_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sids-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Argyle_International_Airport" title="Argyle International Airport">Argyle International Airport</a> is the country's new international airport.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The new facility opened on 14 February 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> replacing the existing <a href="/wiki/E.T._Joshua_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="E.T. Joshua Airport">E.T. Joshua Airport</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2010, Saint Vincent and the Grenadines had 21,700 telephone land lines. Its land telephone system is fully automatic and covers the entire island and all of the inhabited Grenadine islands.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 2002, there were 10,000 mobile phones.<sup id="cite_ref-about_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> By 2010, this number had increased to 131,800.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Mobile phone service is available in most areas of Saint Vincent as well as the Grenadines.
</p><p>Saint Vincent has two ISPs (<a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flow_(brand)" title="Flow (brand)">Flow</a>) that provide cellular telephone and internet service.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Demographics of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Demographics of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<p>The population as estimated in 2016 was 109,643.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The ethnic composition was 66% <a href="/wiki/African_descent" class="mw-redirect" title="African descent">African descent</a>, 19% of mixed descent, 6% East Indian, 4% <a href="/wiki/Europeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Europeans">Europeans</a> (mainly Portuguese), 2% <a href="/wiki/Island_Carib" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Carib">Island Carib</a> and 3% others.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Most Vincentians are the descendants of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">African</a> people brought to the island to work on <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantations</a>. There are other ethnic groups such as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>) and <a href="/wiki/East_India" title="East India">East Indians</a>, both brought in to work on the plantations after the abolishing of slavery by the British living on the island. There is also a growing Chinese population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages_2">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vincentian_Creole" title="Vincentian Creole">Vincentian Creole</a></div>
<p>English is the official language. Most Vincentians speak Vincentian Creole.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> English is used in education, government, religion, and other formal domains, while Creole (or 'dialect' as it is referred to locally) is used in informal situations such as in the home and among friends.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to the 2001 census, 81.5% of the population of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is considered <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>, 6.7% has another religion and 8.8% has no religion or did not state a religion (1.5%).<sup id="cite_ref-2001_census_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001_census-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a> constitutes the largest religious category, with 17.8% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Pentecostals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a> are the second largest group (17.6%). The next largest group are <a href="/wiki/Methodists#Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodists">Methodists</a> (10.9% of the population), followed by <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a> (10.2%) and <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> (10.0%). Other Christians include <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (0.6%), <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> (7.5%), <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelicals</a> (2.8%), Church of God (2.5%), <a href="/wiki/Brethren_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Brethren Christian">Brethren Christian</a> (1.3%), and the <a href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a> (0.3%).
</p><p>Between 1991 and 2001 the number of Anglicans, Brethren, Methodists and Roman Catholics decreased, while the number of Pentecostals, Evangelicals and Seventh-day Adventists increased.
</p><p>The number of non-Christians is small. These religious groups include the <a href="/wiki/Rastafari_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Rastafari movement">Rastafarians</a> (1.5% of the population), <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_West_Indies" title="Hinduism in the West Indies">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mustiquebeaches.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mustiquebeaches.jpg/220px-Mustiquebeaches.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mustiquebeaches.jpg/330px-Mustiquebeaches.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mustiquebeaches.jpg/440px-Mustiquebeaches.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mustiquebeaches.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The island of <a href="/wiki/Mustique" title="Mustique">Mustique</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a></div>
<p>Cricket, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a> and association football are most popular among men whereas <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a> is most popular among women. Basketball, volleyball and tennis are also very popular.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The country's prime <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> league is the <a href="/wiki/NLA_Premier_League" title="NLA Premier League">NLA Premier League</a>, which provides its <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_national_football_team" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines national football team">national (association) football team</a> with most players. A notable Vincentian footballer is <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Hendrickson" title="Ezra Hendrickson">Ezra Hendrickson</a>, former national team captain who played at several Major League Soccer clubs in the United States and is now an assistant coach with the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Sounders_FC" title="Seattle Sounders FC">Seattle Sounders FC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sounders_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sounders-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The country regularly participates at the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Basketball Championship">Caribbean Basketball Championship</a> where a <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_national_basketball_team" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines national basketball team">men's team</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_women%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines women&#39;s national basketball team">women's team</a> compete. Saint Vincent and the Grenadines also has its own <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_national_rugby_union_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines national rugby union team">national rugby union team</a> which is ranked 84th in the world. Other notable sports played at the regional level include track and field.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Music of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Music of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></div>
<p>Music popular in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines includes big drum, <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chutney_music" title="Chutney music">chutney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steelpan" title="Steelpan">steelpan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>. String band music, quadrille and bele music and traditional storytelling are also popular.  One of the most successful St Vincent natives is <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Lyttle" title="Kevin Lyttle">Kevin Lyttle</a>.  He was named Cultural Ambassador for the Island 19 September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The national anthem of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is "<a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent,_Land_so_beautiful" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent, Land so beautiful">Saint Vincent, Land so beautiful</a>", adopted upon independence in 1979.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Saint Vincent has twelve FM radio stations including 88.9 Adoration Fm,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> 89.1 Jem Radio, 89.7 NBC Radio, 95.7 and 105.7 <a href="/wiki/Praise_FM_(Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines)" title="Praise FM (Saint Vincent and the Grenadines)">Praise FM</a>, 96.7 Nice Radio, 97.1 Hot 97, 98.3 Star FM, 99.9 We FM, 103.7 Hitz, 102.7 EZee radio, 104.3 Xtreme FM and 106.9 Boom FM. Several Internet radio stations including Chronicles Christian Radio.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> It has one television broadcast station ZBG-TV (SVGTV)<sup id="cite_ref-svgtv_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-svgtv-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and one cable television provider.
</p><p>St Vincent and the Grenadines Broadcasting Co-operation is the parent company for SVGTV, Magic 103.7.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_Parties">Political Parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Political Parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Unity_Labour_Party" title="Unity Labour Party">Unity Labour Party</a> – In office</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_(Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines)" title="New Democratic Party (Saint Vincent and the Grenadines)">New Democratic Party (Saint Vincent and the Grenadines)</a> – In opposition</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republican_Party_(Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines)" title="Democratic Republican Party (Saint Vincent and the Grenadines)">Democratic Republican Party (Saint Vincent and the Grenadines)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Green_Party" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines Green Party">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines Green Party</a></li></ul>
